{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","title":"AI Investing: The Ultimate Beginner’s Guide","link":"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14978","description":"<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">With artificially intelligent technology on the rise across industries, learning about investing in AI is top-of-mind for many Americans. As people observe the rapid growth of innovative companies utilizing AI tech, there’s been a natural spike in interest around AI </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/category/investing/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">investing</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Predictions that the </span><a href=\"https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/artificial-intelligence-market-size-worth-390-9-billion-by-2025-grand-view-research-inc-300999236.html#:~:text=Men's%20Interest-,Artificial%20Intelligence%20Market%20Size%20Worth%20%24390.9%20Billion,%3A%20Grand%20View%20Research%2C%20Inc.&amp;text=Grand%20View%20Research%2C%20Inc.,-Feb%2005%2C%202020&amp;text=SAN%20FRANCISCO%2C%20Feb.,by%20Grand%20View%20Research%2C%20Inc.\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">AI market size</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> will be worth $390.9 billion by 2025 motivates people to understand more about this business sector.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">From machine learning to pattern recognition and predictive modeling, it’s not easy to keep up with different subsets of artificial intelligence and how they’re impacting businesses. Since AI is such a broad category of technology, sometimes it’s overwhelming to even understand the basics. When you’re considering investing in an AI-driven company, it’s crucial to learn as much as possible about these types of </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/coronavirus-covid-19/why-where-you-put-your-money-matters/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">investments</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. If you’re curious about delving more into the topic of AI investing, check out our guide.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This guide will cover:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"list-style-type: none;\"> \n  <ul> \n   <li style=\"list-style-type: none;\"> \n    <ul> \n     <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14978#investing\">What Is AI Investing?</a></span></li> \n     <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14978#trends\">Trends in AI Investing</a></span></li> \n     <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14978#consider\">Factors to Consider Before Investing in AI</a></span></li> \n     <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14978#shaping\">Companies Shaping the Future of AI Technology</a></span></li> \n     <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14978#additional\">Additional Resources</a></span></li> \n     <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14978#visual\">Jump-to link to infographic</a></li> \n    </ul> </li> \n  </ul> </li> \n</ul> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What Is AI Investing?</span></h2> \n<p><a id=\"investing\"></a><br /> <span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Artificial intelligence (AI) is a series of programs and algorithms that mimic human intelligence to efficiently perform tasks usually completed by humans. The term “artificial intelligence” was </span><a href=\"https://www.livescience.com/49007-history-of-artificial-intelligence.html\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">coined in 1956</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, so AI isn’t a new concept. However, the capabilities of AI have improved drastically over the past two decades, ushering in a new era of technological advancements.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">AI touches almost every aspect of our lives. It’s hard not to notice the influence of AI technology, whether it’s at home with smart devices like Google Home and Amazon’s Alexa, or shopping online with chatbots that recognize our consumer behavior.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">AI investing, or learning how to invest in the AI market, is spiking in popularity thanks to its rapid growth. As AI becomes more integral to various companies and industries, stocks across various industries are becoming more desirable to some investors.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">However, even though research and development in this area are growing exponentially, people still need to be careful about placing bets on developing technology and tools. As with any type of investment, there will always be an element of risk involved when investing in AI.</span><br /> <a id=\"trends\"></a></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Trends in AI Investing&nbsp;</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">With AI investing rapidly spreading across the globe, it’s no wonder that people are paying attention to its growth more than ever. Across various fields, there are </span><a href=\"https://investingnews.com/daily/tech-investing/emerging-tech-investing/artificial-intelligence-investing/artificial-intelligence-investing/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">over 400 use cases and applications for AI</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Leaders in AI development include tech giants like Google, Microsoft, Amazon, and IBM. At the same time, startup funding for lesser-known AI disruptors has been steadily climbing as well.</span></p> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"14980\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/investing/ai-investing/attachment/ai-investing-post-image-1-2/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-1-1.png\" data-orig-size=\"1306,700\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"ai-investing-post-image-1\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-1-1.png?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-1-1.png?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-14980 aligncenter\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-1-1.png\" alt=\"ai-investing-post-image-1\" width=\"640\" height=\"343\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-1-1.png 1306w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-1-1.png?resize=768,412 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-1-1.png?resize=651,349 651w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-1-1.png?resize=595,319 595w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What makes AI investing particularly interesting is its potential to be sustainably lucrative. Banks and financial services firms are building powerful AI strategies and utilizing the technology to streamline fraud detection, wealth management, underwriting, and more. In </span><a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/cognitiveworld/2020/06/06/ai-transforming-the-construction-industry/#2dad2b9274f1\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">construction</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and manufacturing, AI can streamline products and experiences. AI also majorly impacts industries in healthcare, education, and safety.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Three main signs indicating AI investing trends are the following:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://emerj.com/ai-sector-overviews/ai-in-banking-analysis/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">America’s top banks</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> are using AI now more than ever before.</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/blakemorgan/2019/01/24/the-7-best-examples-of-artificial-intelligence-to-improve-personalization/#342110693c4e\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">America’s top companies</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> are using AI technology to improve personalization and customer experience.</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://venturebeat.com/2020/01/22/cb-insights-ai-startup-funding-hit-new-high-of-26-6-billion-in-2019/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Funding for AI startups</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> has been steadily climbing over the past decade.&nbsp;</span></li> \n</ul> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Factors to Consider Before Investing in AI</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Before diving into the world of AI investing, it helps to consider both qualitative and quantitative factors. The ability to find quality investments based on market opportunities isn’t enough, because even solid, profitable companies can be a poor financial investment if the stock prices are too high for you. To position yourself to wisely purchase AI stocks with strong return potential, understand performance and valuation metrics.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Before you decide if an AI-driven company is worth your investment, you’ll probably want to take note of the following:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li><b>Research companies fully. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Understand a company’s business plan and its track record for success so far. What are their guidelines and processes, where are their headquarters and manufacturing facilities, and what are their growth plans for the future?</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>Look for the company’s price-to-earnings ratio. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Even if you feel strongly about investing in a company, don’t let those emotions cause you to give them the benefit of the doubt. When it comes to their financials, you need to understand the ins and outs. How much debt do they have? Are they currently profitable? Understand the current share price relative to its per-share earnings, too.</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>Figure out how much risk is involved.</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> How can you tell how much risk is involved with one company’s stock compared to the rest of the market? You can start by determining a company’s beta, or measure of volatility in relation to the broader market, before investing any funds. </span><a href=\"https://www.investopedia.com/articles/personal-finance/050515/how-calculate-beta-private-company.asp\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Calculating a company’s beta</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> isn’t difficult, and it can save you trouble in the long run.</span></li> \n <li><b>Determine if the stock has a high enough dividend to be worth it. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors can determine which stocks pay dividends by researching financial news websites. Don’t have false expectations — you shouldn’t expect a dividend from a startup.</span></li> \n <li><b>Keep an eye on the company’s stock chart. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Look for some of the most simple cues from stock charts to gauge price movement. Also, consider how the company would be affected by different economic factors and potential changes to the market it serves.</span></li> \n</ul> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"14981\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/investing/ai-investing/attachment/ai-investing-post-image-2/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-2.png\" https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-2.png?resize=651,349 651w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-2.png?resize=595,319 595w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /><a id=\"shaping\"></a></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Companies Shaping the Future of AI Technology</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Many of the companies providing AI technology through their cloud platforms are household names, like Google, Amazon, IBM, and Microsoft. However, there are still plenty of other companies in other sectors that are shaping the future of AI investing. Below are six of the AI-investing business leaders to keep an eye on. We are not in any way recommending that you invest in these companies, rather these are examples of the leaders in investing in AI.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><b>1) Amazon. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Amazon Web Services offers both consumer and business-oriented AI products and services and many of its professional AI services are built on consumer products. For example, the Amazon Echo brings artificial intelligence into the home through the AI bot, Alexa.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><b>2) Alphabet. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Google’s parent company Alphabet is deeply invested in furthering its AI capabilities, along with acquiring numerous AI startups in the last several years. In addition to using AI to improve its services, a number of AI and machine learning services are sold to businesses via the Google Cloud Platform.</span></p> \n<p><b>3) IBM. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">IBM has always been a leader in AI innovation, but its efforts in recent years are around IBM Watson, including an AI-based cognitive service. IBM has been acquiring multiple AI startups over the years as it competes with other industry leaders in this space like Google.</span></p> \n<p><b>4) Microsoft. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Microsoft has a wide range of AI projects that can benefit both businesses and consumers. For example, Cortana, the digital assistant that comes with Windows, is designed for business clients. On its Azure Cloud Service, Microsoft sells AI services such as bot services, machine learning, and cognitive services.</span></p> \n<p><b>5) Alibaba Cloud. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Alibaba is the top cloud computing platform in Asia. It offers business clients a sophisticated Machine Learning Platform for AI, including an intuitive, user-friendly visual interface.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><b>6) Salesforce. </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Salesforce developed Salesforce Einstein, their artificial intelligence service. Their latest initiative, which includes an extensive team of data scientists, uses machine learning to help employees streamline various tasks. It looks like this technology will also become more widely available in the near future.</span></p> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"14982\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/investing/ai-investing/attachment/ai-investing-post-image-3/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-3.png\" data-orig-size=\"1306,700\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"ai-investing-post-image-3\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-3.png?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-3.png?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-14982 aligncenter\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-3.png\" alt=\"ai-investing-post-image-3\" width=\"640\" height=\"343\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-3.png 1306w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-3.png?resize=768,412 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-3.png?resize=651,349 651w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-3.png?resize=595,319 595w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /><a id=\"additional\"></a></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Additional Resources</span></h2> \n<p>There are tons of helpful resources for decision-making about investing in AI. Regardless of how financially savvy you are, there’s always more to learn about how to invest in the most efficient way possible. Your <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/investing/how-to-strengthen-your-investment-portfolio-in-a-volatile-market/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">financial portfolio</a> should be as diverse and robust as possible to set you up for long-term success.</p> \n<p>One of the best ways to start the process of educating yourself is by reading free insights from reputable technology and finance research publications. Try reading <a href=\"https://www.marketwatch.com/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">MarketWatch</a> and <a href=\"https://www.morningstar.com/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Morningstar</a> on a daily basis to keep track of the latest and most accurate company information. By analyzing a company’s financials with a critical eye before making investment decisions, you’ll protect your personal financial health.<br /> <a id=\"visual\"></a><br /> <img data-attachment-id=\"15014\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/investing/ai-investing/attachment/ai-investing-2/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-1.gif\" data-orig-size=\"1306,6834\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"ai-investing-gif\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-1.gif?w=57\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-1.gif?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-15014 aligncenter\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-1.gif\" alt=\"ai-investing-gif\" width=\"640\" height=\"3349\" /></p> \n<p>&nbsp;</p> \n<p>We hope this piece could be a solid introduction to some of the concepts and trends that explain why AI has promising potential in the world of investing. AI investing presents various exciting possibilities for the future, but investors should still proceed with caution. When it comes to <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/planning/investment-calculator/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">investing</a>, always do your due diligence to avoid losing money. AI technology is seamlessly integrated into aspects of almost every industry. Focus on <a href=\"https://www.mint.com/how-mint-works/budgets\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">budgeting</a> and consider investment decisions that are best for your long-term financial health.</p> \n<p><b>Sources: </b><a href=\"https://techjury.net/blog/ai-statistics/#gref\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span +0000","feedId":1636,"bgimg":"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-1-1.png","linkMd5":"061a34b17f4b1024ee0dd1f598a4bc0f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn84@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-18-564_5cfd6d1407377bea.webp","destWidth":1306,"destHeight":700,"sourceBytes":51062,"destBytes":39828,"author":"Mint.com","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-1-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn84@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-18-564_5cfd6d1407377bea.webp","https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-2.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn41@2020_4/2020/08/24/14-32-43-269_8688a90f4b646c25.webp","https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-post-image-3.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn66@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-32-43-328_a01e6a0b0f740a24.webp","https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/ai-investing-1.gif":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=UQKwtqyqtpA:fKnKqPwmlmw:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn33@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-42-174_9ecb878f83c2133b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=UQKwtqyqtpA:fKnKqPwmlmw:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn61@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-42-221_d5abd79da253b869.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=UQKwtqyqtpA:fKnKqPwmlmw:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn57@2020_4/2020/08/24/14-32-42-081_92c23a0b08fd93de.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=UQKwtqyqtpA:fKnKqPwmlmw:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn23@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-32-42-218_87020f8481ecc838.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=dnMXMwOfBR0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn38@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-43-084_e538087722dd60e5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn17@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-43-174_4a59b36f6bebab35.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MyMint/~4/UQKwtqyqtpA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn85@2020_1/2020/08/24/14-32-43-095_37f987a3aefbc70d.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598279537144},{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","title":"What Different States Are Saving For According to Google","link":"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14868","description":"<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As our lifestyles and </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/how-mint-works/budgets\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">budgets</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> have drastically changed since the start of the COVID-19 pandemic, many of us have found ourselves spending less and saving more. With the </span><a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/americans-are-saving-more-but-how-long-can-it-last-11591272180\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">personal savings rate</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> in the US hitting a record high of 33 percent, it’s clear that consumers’ priorities have shifted. We decided to dive into Google search data to figure out which long-term savings goals were most important to people in different states across America.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To find out, we compiled some of the top Google searches from the SEO analysis tool Ahrefs related to saving money. Then, we picked five of the top savings-related terms over the last 12 months to analyze using the tool Google Trends, allowing us to determine Americans’ savings goals in different states. These top goals included saving for a car, college, house, retirement, and an </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/6-ways-to-bolster-your-emergency-fund-by-500/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">emergency fund</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. We showcased our findings in the illustrations below.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Our high-level findings include:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Searches around saving for retirement topped the list, followed by saving for a house.</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">States in the Midwest and the Northeast were most concerned with saving for retirement, with New York, Iowa, Wisconsin, Massachusetts, and Nebraska in the top five.</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Western states are searching for how to save for a house more than states in any other region, with Colorado, Utah, and Idaho ranking in the top three.</span></li> \n</ul> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What Savings Topics are States Searching for the Most?</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Google search data shows that people searching for information related to retirement savings and saving for a house significantly outnumber people searching about other savings goals.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Could Americans be having a change in heart when it comes to retirement savings? Could increased interest in saving for a house in the West be a byproduct of the mass exodus from coastal cities post-COVID-19? Take a look at the various search volumes of savings-related Google searches to gauge how collective interest in saving overpowers the desire to spend on non-essentials.</span></p> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"14869\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/what-different-states-are-saving-for/attachment/top-searches/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/top-searches.gif\" data-orig-size=\"1306,2079\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"top-savings-related-searches\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/top-searches.gif?w=188\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/top-searches.gif?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-14869 aligncenter\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/top-searches.gif\" alt=\"top-savings-related-searches\" width=\"640\" height=\"1019\" /></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">States Most Concerned With Retirement Savings</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Although the Midwest and the Northeast have quite different costs of living, states in these two regions are considered most concerned with saving for retirement according to Google. Regardless of their current living expenses, Internet search interest in long-term savings goals trumps interest in discretionary spending.</span></p> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"14870\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/what-different-states-are-saving-for/attachment/states-most-interseted-in-saving-for-retirement/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/states-most-interseted-in-saving-for-retirement.gif\" data-orig-size=\"1306,1120\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"states-most-interseted-in-saving-for-retirement\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/states-most-interseted-in-saving-for-retirement.gif?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/states-most-interseted-in-saving-for-retirement.gif?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-14870 aligncenter\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/states-most-interseted-in-saving-for-retirement.gif\" alt=\"states-most-interseted-in-saving-for-retirement\" width=\"640\" height=\"549\" /></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">With increased concern regarding health and security in the wake of the pandemic, it’s no surprise that people across the country are reevaluating their saving habits. After all, the US doesn’t have the strongest track record when it comes to saving for retirement.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to the </span><a href=\"https://www.epi.org/publication/the-state-of-american-retirement-savings/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Economic Policy Institute</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> (EPI), most American families — including those approaching the age of retirement — have minimal retirement savings. In fact, the EPI’s 2016 study found that nearly half of all working-age families have zero retirement account savings, while the median (50th percentile) family had only $7,800 saved in these accounts. </span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Even most workers in the top 10 percentile do not have enough in savings to maintain their </span><a href=\"https://www.economicpolicyresearch.org/images/docs/research/retirement_security/Report_Final_The_Retirement_Crisis_in_NY_.pdf\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">standard of living in retirement</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> — the median balance nationwide for this group is $200,000. Hopefully, Americans will keep up the momentum with prioritizing saving post-pandemic. One major challenge will be not </span><a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/05/23/26-percent-of-americans-are-raiding-their-retirement-accounts-after-job-loss.html\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">dipping into their retirement funds</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> during periods of financial stress.</span></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">States Where Saving for a House is the Priority</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">We found that people from Western states had the highest intent of saving for a home, with the top three most interested states being Colorado, Utah, and Idaho.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"14871\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/what-different-states-are-saving-for/attachment/states-most-interested-in-saving-for-a-house/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/states-most-interested-in-saving-for-a-house.gif\" data-orig-size=\"1306,1115\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"states-most-interested-in-saving-for-a-house\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/states-most-interested-in-saving-for-a-house.gif?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/states-most-interested-in-saving-for-a-house.gif?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-14871 aligncenter\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/states-most-interested-in-saving-for-a-house.gif\" alt=\"states-most-interested-in-saving-for-a-house\" width=\"640\" height=\"546\" /></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">With lower mortgage interest rates due to the ongoing pandemic, </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">prospective home buyers are getting into bidding wars over high demand and low supply. According to a report from the Colorado Association of Realtors, buyers have been quickly jumping on </span><a href=\"https://www.cpr.org/2020/07/10/colorado-home-buyers-still-hungry-for-limited-inventory/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">limited inventory</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> now since strict stay-at-home orders were lifted.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">However, with </span><a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/06/05/your-money/houses-prices-coronavirus.html\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">home prices</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> on the rise nationwide, it makes sense that people would be fervently saving in order to afford the house of their choice. When you consider how expensive home prices are, it’s unsurprising that saving for a downpayment must be a financial priority. </span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This is especially true for residents of Hawaii and California, states that ranked #4 and #9 respectively for the highest volume of searches related to saving to buy a house. Hawaii and California are two of the states where saving for a down payment takes the longest. Not only are the houses pricey, but also renting in these states often won’t save you a considerable amount compared to getting a mortgage.</span></p> \n<p>&nbsp;</p> \n<div class=\"table-container\" style=\"display: flex; flex-direction: column; overflow: auto; width: 100%; margin-bottom: 15px; margin-top: 20px;\"> \n <div class=\"table-responsive\">\n  <table style=\"border-collapse: collapse; font-family: 'Avenir', sans-serif; text-align: center; font-size: 18px; color: black; border: 1px solid black;\">Nebraska</td> \n     <td style=\"padding: 20px; text-align: center; font-size: 18px; color: black; border: 1px solid black;\">$29,965</td> \n    </tr> \n    <tr style=\"background-color: #e7e7e8;\"> \n     <td style=\"padding: 20px; text-align: center; font-size: 18px; color: black; border: 1px solid black;\">Wisconsin</td> \n     <td style=\"padding: 20px; text-align: center; font-size: 18px; color: black; border: 1px solid black;\">$40,535</td> \n    </tr> \n    <tr style=\"background-color: #fcfcfc;\"> \n     <td style=\"padding: 20px; text-align: center; font-size: 18px; color: black; border: 1px solid black;\">Nevada</td> \n     <td style=\"padding: 20px; text-align: center; font-size: 18px; color: black; border: 1px solid black;\">$61,946</td> \n    </tr> \n   </tbody> \n  </table>\n </div> \n <div class=\"table-info\"> \n  <p style=\"margin: 0; font-style: italic; background-color: #e7e7e8; padding: 20px; border: 1px solid black; border-top: .5px solid black;\">*An estimated median savings per month (20%) based on the median household income per state is used to determine how many months it would take to save for a 20% deposit based on each state’s median home value.</p> \n </div> \n</div> \n<p>&nbsp;</p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Although different states are prioritizing different types of savings and investments, it’s clear that there has been an increased collective interest in saving over the past year. It’s interesting to consider the role of the pandemic in contributing to </span><a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/05/29/us-savings-rate-hits-record-33percent-as-coronavirus-causes-americans-to-stockpile-cash-curb-spending.html\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“forced savings”</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. As a result of nationwide shutdowns, there are fewer natural opportunities to spend money and Americans are honing in on saving to be more prepared for their futures.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There’s no question that Americans are refocusing on the importance of having a financial safety net in preparation for crises like COVID-19. As the pandemic wears on, it gives people opportunities to </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/how-to-budget/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">develop budgeting habits</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> and prioritize their financial health. With the right mindset and</span> <a href=\"https://www.mint.com/how-mint-works/budgets\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">budget</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, reaching a huge savings goal is feasible for anyone.</span></p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Methodology</span></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">First, we gathered some of the top Google searches from </span><a href=\"https://ahrefs.com/dashboard\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Ahrefs</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> related to saving money. Next, we analyzed the search volumes of these savings-related terms in different states using </span><a href=\"https://trends.google.com/trends/?geo=US\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Google Trends</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. This allowed us to determine which savings goals are the most important to people in different states, according to their Google searches. These goals included saving for a car, college, house, retirement, and an emergency fund.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/what-different-states-are-saving-for/\">What Different States Are Saving For According to Google</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com\">MintLife Blog</a>.</p> \n<div class=\"feedflare\"> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=53-S2uHNpP4:d57JG2BKHmc:D7DqB2pKExk\"><img +0000","feedId":1636,"bgimg":"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/top-searches.gif","linkMd5":"ec0ef8e909f577f14dc5a99798178b14","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn65@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-39-161_cd13df9e6119e242.webp","destWidth":1306,"destHeight":2079,"sourceBytes":1569866,"destBytes":3404668,"author":"Mint.com","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/top-searches.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn65@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-39-161_cd13df9e6119e242.webp","https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/states-most-interseted-in-saving-for-retirement.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn77@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-32-55-337_fb4c2cbbb6085d22.webp","https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/states-most-interested-in-saving-for-a-house.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn61@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-33-07-590_cf6b82a52c87fb49.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=53-S2uHNpP4:d57JG2BKHmc:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn43@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-42-183_3ae6a7c947f8ac21.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=53-S2uHNpP4:d57JG2BKHmc:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn1@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-32-42-274_5a02202988981c2f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=53-S2uHNpP4:d57JG2BKHmc:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn29@2020_6/2020/08/24/14-32-42-178_898eaac30b3d3290.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=53-S2uHNpP4:d57JG2BKHmc:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn53@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-43-269_d9a5a81cce1bc8aa.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=dnMXMwOfBR0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn38@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-43-084_e538087722dd60e5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn17@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-43-174_4a59b36f6bebab35.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MyMint/~4/53-S2uHNpP4":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn7@2020_4/2020/08/24/14-32-42-133_fab91d1516f8cf05.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598279537145},{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","title":"How to Get Extra Money From Bank Signup Bonuses","link":"https://blog.mint.com/?p=15020","description":"<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There are two different ways to balance your budget and </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/how-to/10-tips-to-living-within-your-means-0813/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">live within your means</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The first way is to trim back your expenses. This is the easiest method to get started, but you quickly reach a point of diminishing returns. After all, there are only so many gym memberships or soy lattes that you can cut out. The other method to live within your means is to increase your income.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There are many ways to </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/early-career/increase-your-earning-potential/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">increase your earning potential</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> at your main job, but it’s also possible to get extra money through side hustles and other small sources of extra money. In this article, we’re going to talk about earning extra money through bank checking and savings account signup offers. With a little bit of knowledge and minimal effort, it is possible to earn hundreds if not thousands of dollars per year in bank signup bonuses for new checking and savings accounts.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>What are bank signup bonuses, and why do banks offer them?</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There are many banks out there, and they’re all constantly looking for new customers. Banks have a variety of different marketing channels to attract customers, and there is a cost associated with each one. Just like with </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/credit-cards/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">credit card welcome offers</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, banks want to incentivize you to check out their bank, with the hope that you will like what you see and keep your money with them.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To help do that, many banks offer welcome bonuses for creating either a new checking or savings account. Some banks offer these bonuses only periodically, while others offer new bonuses all of the time. Some bank signup bonuses are publicly available to anyone, while in other cases, you must be specifically targeted (usually by email or direct mail). The amount of a given bank bonus varies with a lot of factors, including how big the bank is or how much money they require you to keep on deposit, but most range between $100 and $500. Also keep in mind that these bonuses are offered per ACCOUNT, so if you have a spouse or partner, you can often both qualify for the bonus to get twice as much.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Common bank account requirements</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In order to get a new account bonus from opening up a bank checking or savings account, you will generally have to meet a certain set of criteria. The criteria differ from bank to bank and from bonus to bonus. Here are a few of the common requirements you may need to meet:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>Deposit</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – Most bank bonuses require that you move a specified amount of money into the bank, and keep it there for a certain amount of time. The amount of money can range from $500 to $10,000 or more, and sometimes the bonus amount varies with how much money you deposit.&nbsp;</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>Direct Deposit</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – Oftentimes, in addition to moving money into the account, you’ll be required to set up one or more direct deposits.&nbsp;</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>Debit card transactions</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – You may also be required to make a certain amount of monthly debit card transactions</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>Bill payments</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> – Or you could be required to make a certain number of bill payments in order to achieve the bonus.</span></li> \n</ul> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The requirements vary by bonus, so it pays to look around. One of the tricks is to look for new bank account bonuses that pay the highest amounts while requiring the least amount of work.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Bank fees and how to avoid them</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Of course, nobody likes bank fees, and we recommend </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/how-to/how-to-avoid-rising-bank-fees/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">avoiding bank fees</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> whenever possible. In the case of bank account bonuses though, it may make sense. After all, even if your new account has a $12 monthly service charge, it might be worth paying that for 3 months while you are waiting for your $300 new account bonus to post! Just remember to close that account after your bonus posts (or look for a way to avoid the monthly surcharges).</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Make sure to check the fine print when you sign up for a new account. Some banks may charge an early termination fee as well. For example, you may need to have your money in your account for three months to get a bonus but if you close your account within SIX months you’re hit with a $100 early termination fee. If that’s the case, make sure to keep your money in the new account at least long enough to avoid any fees.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Tips for staying organized</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While there is nothing particularly difficult about the process, it does require a bit of organization. You won’t need anything too complicated – a simple spreadsheet or date-based reminder system will be sufficient for most people. Just keep track of when you’ve opened an account, what bonus you’re expecting, and when it’s safe to remove your money.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s also important to understand that in almost all cases you will be receiving a 1099-INT form at the end of the year. The money you receive from a new account bonus is considered interest, and it is taxable. The bank won’t withhold any tax from the bonus, so that may adjust the size of your refund or how much tax you owe when it comes time to file your tax return.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>The bottom line</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Bank account bonuses can be a lucrative way to earn a bit of extra money with not a lot of effort. Rather than keep your money in a checking or savings account earning next to zero interest, with a little bit of organization you can start to really put that money to work.</span></p> \n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com/how-to/how-to-get-extra-money-from-bank-signup-bonuses/\">How to Get Extra Money From Bank Signup Bonuses</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com\">MintLife Blog</a>.</p> \n<div class=\"feedflare\"> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=Y9TXG8Hi12M:VVEUfDQZA0o:D7DqB2pKExk\"><img \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In this post, we’re taking you through the steps of budgeting using the 50/30/20 approach so that you can learn&nbsp;</span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/budgeting/budgeting-101/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">how to set up a budget</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&nbsp;that’s sustainable, effective, and simple. Use the links below to navigate or read all the way through to absorb all of our tips on how to budget using the 50/30/20 method:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"list-style-type: none;\"> \n  <ul> \n   <li><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com?p=54305&amp;preview_id=54305#budgeting-rule\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What is the 50/30/20 Budgeting Rule</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">?</span> \n    <ul> \n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com?p=54305&amp;preview_id=54305#essentials\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Essentials: 50% of your income</span></a></li> \n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com?p=54305&amp;preview_id=54305#wants\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Wants: 30% of your income</span></a></li> \n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com?p=54305&amp;preview_id=54305#savings\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Savings: 20% of your income</span></a></li> \n    </ul> </li> \n   <li><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com?p=54305&amp;preview_id=54305#ask-yourself\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Ask Yourself: Why is a 50/30/20 Budget Necessary?</span></a></li> \n   <li><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com?p=54305&amp;preview_id=54305#how-to-budget\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">How to Budget with the 50/30/20 Rule</span></a></li> \n   <li><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com?p=54305&amp;preview_id=54305#right-for-you\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Is the 50/30/20 Budget Right for You?</span></a></li> \n   <li><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com?p=54305&amp;preview_id=54305#main-takeaways\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Main Takeaways: How to Budget with 50/30/20</span></a></li> \n  </ul> </li> \n</ul> \n<h2 id=\"budgeting-rule\"><b>What is the 50/30/20 Budgeting Rule?</b></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Popularized by Senator Elizabeth Warren and her daughter, the 50/30/20 budgeting rule–also referred to as the 50/20/30 budgeting rule–divides after-tax income into three different buckets:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Essentials (50%)</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Wants (30%)</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Savings (20%)</span></li> \n</ul> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"13428\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/how-to-budget/attachment/graphic-2-edit/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Graphic-2-edit.png\" data-orig-size=\"727,563\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"Graphic 2 edit\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Graphic-2-edit.png?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Graphic-2-edit.png?w=727\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\" wp-image-13428 aligncenter\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Graphic-2-edit.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"693\" height=\"537\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Graphic-2-edit.png 727w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Graphic-2-edit.png?resize=451,349 451w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Graphic-2-edit.png?resize=412,319 412w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 693px) 100vw, 693px\" /></p> \n<h3 id=\"essentials\"><b>Essentials: 50% of your income</b></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To begin abiding by this rule, set aside no more than half of your income for the absolute necessities in your life. This might seem like a high percentage (and, at 50%, it is), but once you consider everything that falls into this category it begins to make a bit more sense.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Your essential expenses are those you would almost certainly have to pay, regardless of where you lived, where you worked, or what your future plans happen to include. In general, these expenses are nearly the same for everyone and include:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Housing</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Food</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Transportation costs</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Utility bills</span></li> \n</ul> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The percentage lets you adjust, while still maintaining a sound, balanced budget. And remember, it’s more about the total sum than individual costs. For instance, some people live in high-rent areas, yet can walk to work, while others enjoy much lower housing costs, but transportation is far more expensive.</span></p> \n<h3 id=\"wants\"><b>Wants: 30% of your income</b></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The second category, and the one that can make the most difference in your budget, is unnecessary expenses that enhance your lifestyle. Some financial experts consider this category completely discretionary, but in modern society, many of these so-called luxuries have taken on more of a mandatory status. It all depends on what you want out of life and what you’re willing to sacrifice.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">These personal lifestyle expenses include items such as: your cell phone plan, cable bill and trips to the coffee shop. If you travel extensively or work on-the-go, your cell phone plan is probably more of a necessity than a luxury. However, you have some wiggle room since you can decide upon the tier of the service you’re paying for. Other components of this category include gym memberships, weekend trips, and dining out with your friends. Only you can decide which of your expenses can be designated as “personal,” and which ones are truly obligatory. Similar to how no more than 50 percent of your income should go toward essential expenses, 30 percent is the maximum amount you should spend on personal choices. The fewer costs you have in this category, the more progress you’ll make paying down debt and securing your future.</span></p> \n<h3 id=\"savings\"><b>Savings: 20% of your income</b></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The next step is to dedicate 20% of your take-home pay toward savings. This includes savings plans, retirement accounts, debt payments and rainy-day funds—things you should add to, but which wouldn’t endanger your life or leave you homeless if you didn’t. That’s a bit of an oversimplification, but hopefully you get the gist. This category of expenses should only be paid after your essentials are already taken care of and before you even think about anything in the last category of personal spending.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Think of this as your “get ahead” category. Whereas 50%(or less) of your income is the goal for essentials, 20 percent—or more—should be your goal as far as obligations are concerned. You’ll pay off debt quicker and make more significant strides toward a frustration-free future by devoting as much of your income as you can to this category.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The term “retirement” might not carry a sense of urgency when you’re only 24 years old, but it certainly will become more pressing in decades to come. Just keep in mind the advantage of starting early is you will earn compounding interest the longer you let this fund grow.</span></p> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"11223\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/how-to-budget/attachment/3-3/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/3.jpg\" data-orig-size=\"1000,667\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"3\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/3.jpg?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/3.jpg?w=1000\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-11223 aligncenter\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/3.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"427\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/3.jpg 1000w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/3.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/3.jpg?resize=523,349 523w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/3.jpg?resize=478,319 478w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Establishing good habits will last a lifetime. You don’t need a high income to follow the tenets of the 50/30/20 rule; anyone can do it. Since this is a percentage-based system, the same proportions apply whether you’re earning an&nbsp;</span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/early-career/5-tips-on-how-to-negotiating-an-entry-level-salary-050416/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">entry-level salary</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&nbsp;and living in a studio apartment, or if you’re years into your career and about to buy your first home.</span></p> \n<p><b>A note of caution, though:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&nbsp;Try not to take this rule too literally. The proportions are sound, but your life is unlike anyone else’s. What this plan does is provide a framework for you to work within. Once you review your income and expenses and determine what’s essential and what’s not, only then you can create a budget that helps you make the most of your money. Years from now, you can still fall back on the same guidelines to help your budget evolve as your life does.</span></p> \n<h2 id=\"ask-yourself\"><b>Ask Yourself: Why is a 50/30/20 Budget Necessary?</b></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to&nbsp;</span><a href=\"https://www.consumer.gov/articles/1002-making-budget\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Consumer.gov</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, there are plenty of different reasons why people start a budget:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To save up for a large expense such as a house, car, or vacation</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Put a security deposit on an apartment</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To reduce spending habits</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To improve credit score&nbsp;</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To eliminate debt</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To break the paycheck to paycheck cycle</span></li> \n</ul> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Identifying the reason why&nbsp;</span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">you’re</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&nbsp;budgeting with the 50/30/20 method can help you stay motivated and create a better plan to reach your goal. It’s kind of like the “eye on the prize” mentality. If you’re tempted to splurge, you can use your overarching goal to bring you back to your saving senses. So ask yourself: why am I starting to budget? What do I want to achieve?&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Additionally, if you’re saving up for something specific, try to determine an exact number so that you can regularly evaluate whether or not your budget is on track throughout the week, month, or year.</span></p> \n<h2 id=\"how-to-budget\"><b>How to Budget with the 50/30/20 Rule</b></h2> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"13429\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/how-to-budget/attachment/larger/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Larger.png\" data-orig-size=\"653,352\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"Larger\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Larger.png?w=300\" https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Larger.png?resize=647,349 647w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/Larger.png?resize=592,319 592w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 813px) 100vw, 813px\" /></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To make the most of this budgeting method, consider following the steps below:</span></p> \n<h3><b>Deep Dive Into Your Current Spending Habits</b></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Before implementing a 50/30/20 budget, take a long, hard look in the mirror (or maybe your wallet, rather). We’re talking about analyzing your spending habits. Do you overspend on clothes? Shoes? Food? Drinks? Figuring out your spending vices from the very beginning will help you learn how to use a 50/30/20 budget that effectively cuts spending where you need it most.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Take a look at your bank and credit card statements over the last few months and see if you can find any common trends. If you find that you’re overspending on going out for food and drinks, come up with a plan for how you can avoid this scenario. Cook dinner at home before, have a potluck with friends, find happy hour specials around town. There are plenty of ways to budget and save money without compromising your social life.</span></p> \n<p><b><i>Pro Tip:</i></b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&nbsp;Using Mint’s&nbsp;</span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/how-mint-works/categorization#toc\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">easy budget categorization</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, you can identify where you can cut back on unnecessary expenses.</span></p> \n<h3><b>Identify Irregular Large Ticket Expenses in the “Wants” Category</b></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Of course, there are expenses in life that we simply can’t avoid. Maybe you need to make a repair on your vehicle, or perhaps you’re putting a down payment on a house in the next six months. Oftentimes these&nbsp;</span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/how-mint-works/bills#toc\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">bills</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&nbsp;are necessary expenses, so you’ll have to factor them into your budget.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">When you’re coming up with your 50/30/20 budget, take a moment to look at your calendar so that you can plan for these expenses and adjust your spending in the time before and after you incur the expense.</span></p> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"11222\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/how-to-budget/attachment/2-3/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2.jpg\" data-orig-size=\"1000,667\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"2\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2.jpg?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2.jpg?w=1000\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-11222 aligncenter\" https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2.jpg?resize=523,349 523w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/2.jpg?resize=478,319 478w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></p> \n<h3><b>Add Up All Income</b></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Totaling your income is an important first step when learning how to budget your money using the 50/30/20 rule, but it’s not always as simple as it sounds. Depending on your job, you might have a relatively steady paycheck or one that fluctuates from month to month. If the latter is the case, collect your paychecks from the last six months and find the average income between them.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<h2 id=\"right-for-you\"><b>Is the 50/30/20 Budget Right for You?</b></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The 50/30/20 budget isn’t the only option. Other popular methods include:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>Zero-sum:&nbsp;</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The principle of the zero-sum budget is that you must allocate each and every dollar you earn toward a specific expense, savings account, debt, or disposable income account. This style can help deter unnecessary spending because you’ll know exactly how much you have to spend on what items.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></li> \n</ul> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>Envelope budgeting:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&nbsp;Swiping your card left and right is easy—but the envelope method doesn’t let you succumb to this temptation. Rather than using your card to spend, you use a predetermined amount of cash as your spending pool, nothing more.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></li> \n</ul> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Choosing a budgeting style that works for you depends on a variety of factors; there’s no one-size-fits-all approach to budgeting and saving money. That said, the 50/30/20 tends to be a simple yet effective option for getting started on your budgeting journey.</span></p> \n<h2><img data-attachment-id=\"11224\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/how-to-budget/attachment/4-3/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/4.jpg\" data-orig-size=\"1000,667\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"4\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/4.jpg?w=300\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/4.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"427\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/4.jpg 1000w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/4.jpg?resize=478,319 478w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></h2> \n<h2 id=\"main-takeaways\"><b>Main Takeaways: How to Budget Using the 50/30/20 Rule</b></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Here are the key tenets of the 50/30/20 rule of budgeting:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This budget rule is a simple method that can help you reach your financial goals</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This budgeting method stipulates that you spend no more than 50% of your after-tax income on needs</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The remaining after-tax income should be split up between 30% wants or “lifestyle” purchases, and 20% to savings or debt repayment</span></li> \n</ul> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mint offers budgeting software and a helpful <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/budgeting/budgeting-calculator/\">budgeting calculator</a> that makes it easy to live in accordance with the 50/30/20 rule (or any budget that suits your lifestyle) so that you can live life to its fullest. After spending just a little bit of time determining which of your expenses fall into which category, you can create your very first budget and keep track of it every day. And when your situation undoubtedly changes, Mint lets you adjust, so your budget can change with you.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><a href=\"https://mint.intuit.com/login.event?task=S&amp;utm_medium=blog&amp;cta=nav_sign_up_dropdown\" target=\"_blank\">Sign up for your free account today</a>, build your 50/30/20 budget, and make this the year you build a strong foundation for your future.</span></p> \n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/how-to-budget/\">50/30/20 Budgeting Rule: How to Use It 14-32-43-166_8c11d26039afb80f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=hEbqoH_bAmc:EfefMkPhbX8:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn29@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-32-43-207_3d701b3baff2e970.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=hEbqoH_bAmc:EfefMkPhbX8:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn25@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-43-177_e1c525a416f52879.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=hEbqoH_bAmc:EfefMkPhbX8:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn87@2020_6/2020/08/24/14-32-42-181_048071bcb72b79f1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=dnMXMwOfBR0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn38@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-43-084_e538087722dd60e5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn17@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-43-174_4a59b36f6bebab35.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MyMint/~4/hEbqoH_bAmc":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn82@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-32-43-062_46d9c5ed932469a1.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598279537147},{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","title":"How to Talk to Your Significant Other About Finances","link":"https://blog.mint.com/?p=15026","description":"<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Money is one of the most important topics to talk about with your significant other, no matter what level your relationship is at. From casual dating to being in a relationship to a married couple, if you’re not on the same page regarding finances, it’s likely to cause stress and/or lead to divorce. According to research conducted by Jeffrey Dew, Ph.D., an assistant professor of Family, Consumer, and Human Development at Utah State University, couples who argue about finances at least once a week were </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/how-to/why-couples-fight/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">30% more likely to divorce than couples who argue about money less often</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">For National Couples Day, in this article, we are going to explore a few ways to talk to your significant other about finances and how to set financial goals as a couple, no matter what kind of couple you are.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Turbo’s #RealMoneyTalk survey</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February 2019, Turbo </span><a href=\"https://www.intuit.com/company/press-room/press-releases/2019/intuit-turbo-launches-realmoneytalk-campaign-featuring-chrissy-metz-to-break-the-taboo-of-talking-about-money/\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">commissioned a survey</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> that was conducted online by The Harris Poll in order to better understand behaviors and attitudes around talking about money-related topics with others.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">One of the findings that came out of that survey was that 90% of people in a relationship said that they are open and honest with their partner about their finances and 85% believe their partner is open and honest with them about their finances. It’s possible however that this is a misperception since 23% also admit they sometimes hide purchases from their partner, 17% admit they have accounts/debt their partner doesn’t need to know about, and 14% of those who have individual debt in their relationship admit they are currently hiding debt from their partner.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>How to talk to your partner about finances while casually dating</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">When you’re only casually dating someone, there is not as much of a need to discuss finances. At this point, it’s likely that your finances are completely separate, with each partner still living on their own and contributing to their own expenses. The only discussions you’re likely to have involve expenses for shared activities.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you and your partner are in a similar financial situation with similarly paying jobs and expenses, then the expenses from these joint activities is an easier calculation. Each partner can plan on paying equally for any shared activities. Where things get more complicated is when you and your partner are not on an even financial footing. If you have a lower-paying job and/or more debt while your partner has a high-paying job and no debt, this can cause friction. Your partner may often suggest more expensive activities than you feel comfortable with. The key here is open communication about your feelings to find out what is the right path for you and your partner.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Talking to your significant other about finances in a serious relationship</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As your relationship progresses, you will want to have more in-depth conversations with your significant other about finances. Start talking about your own financial habits and goals, and observe the habits and goals of your partner. You shouldn’t necessarily try to change your partner, but it can be valuable to talk about your own feelings and experiences. How comfortable you are talking with your partner about money is likely similar to how far your relationship is progressing as a whole.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you start contemplating either moving in together or getting married, it’s important to open up more about your financial situation. This can be a bit of a tricky situation, especially if you and your partner are in wildly different financial situations. It may be tempting to try and hide or downplay negative financial information about yourself (lower-income, amount of debt). But hiding this kind of information can start the relationship off on a bad foot. A better idea is to be open about it and come up with a plan that you both can agree on.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>How married couples can talk about finances with each other</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There are several ways for married couples to organize their finances. Some married couples keep all of their finances completely together, with maybe a small amount for each couple to use as an “allowance”. Other couples have a combined account for shared expenses and then keep separate accounts for personal expenses. In either case, good communication is the most important factor.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to the #RealMoneyTalk survey, those in a relationship do see their partner as financially beneficial. 86% of those surveyed said that they trust their partner to contribute as much as they can to their combined financial well-being.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>How to set financial goals as a couple</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As we’ve said several times in this article, honest and open communication is the key to talking to your significant others as a couple. One good way to make sure you’re both on the same page is to set financial goals as a couple.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Remember, it’s not just about spending. You may be a saver while your partner is a spender. That isn’t necessarily a red flag that should keep you apart – instead, consider a way to compromise. Stay open and honest about your finances and what is important to you.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Starting the conversation by talking about financial goals can be a better way to keep the conversation productive. So instead of complaining about their spending habits, talk about where you see yourselves in 6 months, a year or more. That can help open up the discussion to start discussing more day-to-day topics like budgeting and spending.</span></p> \n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com/how-to/how-to-talk-to-your-significant-other-about-finances/\">How to Talk to Your Significant Other About Finances</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com\">MintLife Blog</a>.</p> \n<div class=\"feedflare\"> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=prMM8KOpSCM:Y-3VhJ2xZxk:D7DqB2pKExk\"><img <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=prMM8KOpSCM:Y-3VhJ2xZxk:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=prMM8KOpSCM:Y-3VhJ2xZxk:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\" /></a> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=prMM8KOpSCM:Y-3VhJ2xZxk:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=prMM8KOpSCM:Y-3VhJ2xZxk:V_sGLiPBpWU\" border=\"0\"
