src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MyMint/~4/prMM8KOpSCM\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\" />","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 18 Aug 2020 18:27:26 +0000","feedId":1636,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=prMM8KOpSCM:Y-3VhJ2xZxk:D7DqB2pKExk","linkMd5":"4ccbc8f89659afbbc7e2ab661689bde8","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn97@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-18-375_105d7ad9558c0713.webp","destWidth":92,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1043,"destBytes":374,"author":"Dan Miller","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=prMM8KOpSCM:Y-3VhJ2xZxk:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn97@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-18-375_105d7ad9558c0713.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=prMM8KOpSCM:Y-3VhJ2xZxk:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn1@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-43-270_cf18dc91ae871f45.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=prMM8KOpSCM:Y-3VhJ2xZxk:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn98@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-32-43-152_6bc5e46f2d276b32.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=prMM8KOpSCM:Y-3VhJ2xZxk:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn11@2020_6/2020/08/24/14-32-42-165_807dfd0afec9b195.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=dnMXMwOfBR0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn38@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-43-084_e538087722dd60e5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn17@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-43-174_4a59b36f6bebab35.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MyMint/~4/prMM8KOpSCM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn38@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-32-42-039_22a47c0491e08800.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598279537143},{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","title":"How Does Credit Card Interest Work?","link":"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14168","description":"<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Credit card interest occurs when a user doesn’t pay their card’s monthly balance in full. The amount you pay on top of each dollar that remains unpaid is considered a card’s “interest rate.” This amount must be stated in the terms and conditions of a card’s application so that you have the information readily available.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To calculate the dollar amount you’ll pay in interest for any given month, follow these steps (which we expand on below):</span></p> \n<ol> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Find your average daily rate&nbsp;</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Find your average daily balance&nbsp;</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Multiply your answers from step 1 and step 2</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Take this number and multiply it by the number of days in the billing cycle</span></li> \n</ol> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Follow along below to dive into a detailed look at how credit card interest works.</span></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">What Is Credit Card Interest?</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Credit card interest is the amount you’ll pay if a balance isn’t paid off by the due date. This is how credit card companies make money. Think of this as the “subscription fee” to borrow their money.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Some cards have high interest rates and some have low rates. Typically, the lower your credit score, the higher the interest rate will be. You should be wary of using cards with high interest rates, as this can quickly compound into high amounts of debt should balances not be paid off in a timely manner. If that’s the case, you may want to consider </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/credit/how-to-cancel-a-credit-card/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">canceling your credit card</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">How Is Credit Card Interest Calculated?</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There are two key elements to factor in when determining your card’s interest rate: average daily rate and average daily balance. When multiplied together, you’ll get the given period’s interest payment — that is, the extra dollar amount you’ll owe should you not pay it off in full.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Here’s an in-depth look at calculating your credit card’s monthly interest payment. We also walk through an example calculation you can easily apply to your personal finances.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"14169\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/credit/how-does-credit-card-interest-work-4/attachment/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1.png\" data-orig-size=\"1306,810\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt (1)\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1.png?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1.png?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-14169\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"397\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1.png 1306w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1.png?resize=768,476 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1.png?resize=563,349 563w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1.png?resize=514,319 514w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">1. Calculate Your Average Daily Rate</span></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">First, you’ll need to calculate the amount of interest you’re paying daily throughout the entire year. Simply divide the annual interest rate (this is usually the percentage a card company will give you in the contract) by 365.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Example: For an </span><b>annual </b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">interest rate of 15%</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Take .15 (annual interest rate) and divide it by 365 (total days in a year)</span> \n  <ul> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.15 / 365 = .00041096&nbsp;</span></li> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Average Daily Rate = .00041096&nbsp;</span></li> \n  </ul> </li> \n</ul> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Write this amount down for use in a couple of steps.</span></p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">2. Calculate Your Average Daily Balance</span></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To calculate your average daily balance, you’ll need your latest credit card statement. Next, follow these steps below:</span></p> \n<ol> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Write down your ending balance day by day</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Add each daily balance together</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Divide the total by the number of days in the current billing cycle</span></li> \n</ol> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Example:&nbsp;</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Add each daily balance together</span> \n  <ul> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Day 1 ending balance: $100&nbsp;</span></li> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">+ Day 2 ending balance: $105 …</span></li> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">+ Day 30 ending balance: $1,000&nbsp;</span></li> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">= $6,100</span></li> \n  </ul> </li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Divide by the total number of days in the billing cycle</span> \n  <ul> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">$6,100 / 30 days = $203.33</span></li> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Average Daily Balance = $203.33</span></li> \n  </ul> </li> \n</ul> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">3. Multiply Average Daily Rate by Average Daily Balance</span></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This step is simple. Multiply your answer from step one and step two.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Example:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Average Daily Rate (from Step 1): .00041096</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Average Daily Balance (from Step 2): $203.33</span> \n  <ul> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.00041096 x $203.33 = .084</span></li> \n  </ul> </li> \n</ul> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">4. Calculate This Cycle’s Interest Owed</span></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Finally, to find the interest payment for a given billing cycle, you’ll want to multiply your answer from step three by the number of days in the billing cycle (this is the same number you used in step two to find your average daily balance).&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Example:&nbsp;</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"list-style-type: none;\"> \n  <ul> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Answer from Step 3: .084</span></li> \n   <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Number of days in the billing cycle: 30</span> \n    <ul> \n     <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.084 x 30 = 2.52</span></li> \n     <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><b>Interest to be paid for this billing cycle = $2.52*</b></li> \n    </ul> </li> \n  </ul> </li> \n</ul> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">*Note: This amount starts compounding each day if the balance is not paid in full.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Interest Rate vs. APR</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">When it comes to credit cards, interest and APR are the </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/credit/what-is-credit-card-apr/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">same</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. With other loans, the interest rate determines the cost of borrowing the amount you request. APR, then, is an annualized rate of interest that includes certain fees as “finance charges.” APR is intended to allow consumers to comparison shop based on the true cost of credit and can give a more accurate view of what to expect.</span></p> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"14170\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/credit/how-does-credit-card-interest-work-4/attachment/credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr-1/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr-1.png\" data-orig-size=\"1306,592\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr (1)\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr-1.png?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr-1.png?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-14170\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"290\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr-1.png 1306w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr-1.png?resize=768,348 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr-1.png?resize=770,349 770w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr-1.png?resize=704,319 704w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">How to Find Your Credit Card Interest Rate</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To find your card’s annual interest rate, look at your contract or application. Remember, it may be listed as APR as the two are interchangeable when referring to credit cards.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The amount will be expressed as a percentage, and this is how much you’ll pay on top of any balance should you not pay off the full amount.</span></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">3 Ways To Avoid Paying Credit Card Interest</span></h2> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"14171\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/credit/how-does-credit-card-interest-work-4/attachment/3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest-1/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest-1.png\" data-orig-size=\"1306,484\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest (1)\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest-1.png?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest-1.png?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-14171\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest-1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"640\" height=\"237\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest-1.png 1306w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest-1.png?resize=768,285 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest-1.png?resize=942,349 942w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest-1.png?resize=861,319 861w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">There are a few strategies that can help you avoid paying high interest on your credit card payments, and in some cases, pay no interest at all.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s important to know these tactics to avoid spiraling into uncontrollable credit card debt. Rember, balances carry over month-to-month and can get exponential in a short period of time.</span></p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Pay Balance In Full</span></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The best way to avoid credit card interest is to pay your balance off completely at the end of each billing period. Because interest is built on remaining balances, without one, there’s nothing to charge for (think of it as multiplying by zero).</span></p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Never Overspend</span></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Only charge what you can realistically pay off at the end of each cycle on your credit card. Even missing one payment can start a domino effect of interest-heavy payments down the line. Stick to a budget and know what you can afford, especially when dealing with credit cards.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Use Your Card For Necessities</span></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To help budget with your credit card, only use it for needs (e.g. </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/food-budgets/how-to-budget-groceries/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">groceries</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">). This money will have to be spent regardless, so make it much easier to avoid interest by paying off the balance at the end of the cycle. This practice also encourages a healthy credit score.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Thoroughly understanding your contract with a credit card company is the best place to start when determining how credit card interest works. Many times it’s a uniform process, however, each company will tack on their own terms and conditions. By understanding the basics highlighted above, you can make more informed decisions about which </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/credit-cards/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">credit cards</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> are best for you.</span></p> \n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com/credit/how-does-credit-card-interest-work-4/\">How Does Credit Card Interest Work?</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com\">MintLife Blog</a>.</p> \n<div class=\"feedflare\"> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=3uTEPiGGnz0:ibR0KofY6jI:D7DqB2pKExk\"><img +0000","feedId":1636,"bgimg":"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1.png","linkMd5":"a6548b8bc4c1695c95aed7bbdbac73a6","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn68@2020_6/2020/08/24/14-32-18-464_e74d60c03c3b7a9b.webp","destWidth":1306,"destHeight":810,"sourceBytes":62991,"destBytes":57912,"author":"Mint.com","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/how-to-calculate-credit-card-interest-alt-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn68@2020_6/2020/08/24/14-32-18-464_e74d60c03c3b7a9b.webp","https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/credit-card-apr-vs-loan-apr-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn22@2020_6/2020/08/24/14-32-42-194_eccc7e580c1178ae.webp","https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/05/3-ways-to-avoid-paying-credit-card-interest-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn4@2020_4/2020/08/24/14-32-42-264_a50d182fe25d0571.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=3uTEPiGGnz0:ibR0KofY6jI:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn75@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-42-712_f1787b3f0c9034f8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=3uTEPiGGnz0:ibR0KofY6jI:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn57@2020_4/2020/08/24/14-32-43-344_8faaf3164d9612dc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=3uTEPiGGnz0:ibR0KofY6jI:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn53@2020_4/2020/08/24/14-32-42-231_9a00c2e5e5e6d1a1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=3uTEPiGGnz0:ibR0KofY6jI:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn11@2020_1/2020/08/24/14-32-42-229_60678aa3c8cbf5da.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=dnMXMwOfBR0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn38@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-43-084_e538087722dd60e5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn17@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-43-174_4a59b36f6bebab35.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MyMint/~4/3uTEPiGGnz0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn93@2020_4/2020/08/24/14-32-43-085_a38d31c79a03e4a5.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598279537145},{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","title":"6 Ways to Find Extra Income (video)","link":"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14940","description":"<p><iframe title=\"Embedded player. Title not set from remote.\" class=\"youtube-player\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/1h8sJY5MSmU?version=3&amp;rel=1&amp;fs=1&amp;autohide=2&amp;showsearch=0&amp;showinfo=1&amp;iv_load_policy=1&amp;wmode=transparent\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" style=\"border:0;\"></iframe></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Living within your means is an important component of having strong and healthy finances. </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/budgeting/budgeting-101/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Creating a budget</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> can be a great first step to making sure your financial house is in order. As you look through your monthly expenses, there are two different ways that you can improve your monthly cash flow.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The first is to cut your expenses – look for ways that you can spend less each month. When you first start tracking your expenses (like with one of our </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/budgeting-3/monthly-budget-template-track-your-spending-by-month\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">free monthly budget templates</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">), you’ll likely find a few areas to cut back on. Over time, however, you’ll probably run out of ways to cut your expenses. After all, there are so many extra lattes and gym memberships that you don’t use!&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The other way you can </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/why-your-savings-rate-may-be-more-important-than-your-rate-of-return-102011/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">increase your savings rate</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> is to find extra income. In this article, we’ll look through a few side hustles and other ways to find extra income.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Sell things you aren’t using and don’t need</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Most people always have things lying around the house that they no longer use. Take a look around with a discerning eye and decide which things you could do without. Of course, this is not something that you can do every day, but at the rate that most people gather things, you can probably find $100 or more in items once or twice per year. Look for electronics, clothes, toys or other things and sell on Craigslist, local barter groups or on eBay.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Capitalize on your talent</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The first item we’ll talk about is dependent on YOU. What makes you special? What kind of skills do you have that might be able to bring in extra income? Many of the other things on this list are more short-term or one-time ideas. Maybe you can start a blog or online business? Or do you have a skill that you could provide to others as a service? It may take some short-term capital to get your business up and running, but the long-term gains from investing in yourself are usually worth it.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Make sure your savings dollars are working for you</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Another way that you can find some additional money each month is by making sure that your savings dollars are invested in the right place. If you have extra money already stored up, you’ll want to make sure it isn’t sitting under your mattress or in a checking account earning next to no interest. For money that you don’t expect to need any time soon, consider </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/ira-center/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">opening a retirement account</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Historically and with a long-term perspective, the stock market has been one of the best avenues for investments.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you have </span><a href=\"https://blog.turbotax.intuit.com/income-and-investments/emergency-fund-guide-why-everyone-should-have-one-45364/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">an emergency fund</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> or other money, you won’t want to put it in the stock market. Because the stock market can be more volatile, any money that you want to have easier access to should be kept in something that is more liquid. But if you still have your money in a savings account at your local bank, you might be leaving tens to hundreds of dollars on the table each month. Many </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/savings-accounts/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">online savings accounts</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> generally offer savings rates 10 to 20 times as much as the rates you’ll get from your local bank.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Open a new bank account</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Speaking of bank accounts, many banks have incentives for opening a new account. And they’re often better gifts than the stereotypical toaster. A typical bank bonus might be between $200 and $500, depending on the requirements involved. You can find these bonuses by either searching online or looking at local and national banks to see what they might be offering.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Three things to keep in mind with bank account bonuses. The first is that many of these bank bonuses have requirements like setting up a direct deposit or keeping your money in for a certain period of time. Another is that many of these accounts have fees, which would offset some of the bonuses. Finally, the bonus you earn from this account is taxable; you’ll get a 1099 tax form at the end of the year. Weigh all these factors to decide if the bonus is worth it to you.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Maximize your credit card rewards</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Another way to get some extra income is to make sure that you are maximizing your credit card rewards. Credit card rewards can be a good source of extra income depending on your spending levels. In addition to the cashback or rewards you get from ongoing spending, look at signing up for a new credit card. </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/credit-cards/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Many cards offer signup bonuses</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> anywhere from $150 to $500 or more. This can be a great source of additional income.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Join the gig economy</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Depending on how much free time you have, there are many companies out there that are looking for workers. Some ideas would be:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Rent out part of your house with Airbnb</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Drive for Uber or Lyft</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Make deliveries with DoorDash or Postmates</span></li> \n</ul> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Many of these companies also offer new hire incentives that might make the gig seem more attractive at first.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Hopefully, these ideas to get extra income will help spark you as you look for ways to earn more money, balance your budget and get yourself set on the road to financial success!</span></p> href=\"https://blog.mint.com\">MintLife Blog</a>.</p> \n<div class=\"feedflare\"> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=AFyudhZZF6k:xLg9XMFvVZw:D7DqB2pKExk\"><img href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=AFyudhZZF6k:xLg9XMFvVZw:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\" /></a> \n</div>\n<img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MyMint/~4/AFyudhZZF6k\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\" />","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 07 Aug 2020 18:08:23 +0000","feedId":1636,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=AFyudhZZF6k:xLg9XMFvVZw:D7DqB2pKExk","linkMd5":"5a8820e77765e0099418a0a896b495df","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn77@2020_6/2020/08/24/14-32-18-363_3aef91631d0fc0e6.webp","destWidth":92,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":1043,"destBytes":374,"author":"Dan Miller","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=AFyudhZZF6k:xLg9XMFvVZw:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn77@2020_6/2020/08/24/14-32-18-363_3aef91631d0fc0e6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=AFyudhZZF6k:xLg9XMFvVZw:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn51@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-42-247_1062c8e65ccec94c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=AFyudhZZF6k:xLg9XMFvVZw:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn45@2020_2/2020/08/24/14-32-43-282_ee73167b1c0d5b9a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=AFyudhZZF6k:xLg9XMFvVZw:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn31@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-42-183_000f3a44bf644db3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=dnMXMwOfBR0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn38@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-43-084_e538087722dd60e5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn17@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-43-174_4a59b36f6bebab35.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MyMint/~4/AFyudhZZF6k":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn39@2020_4/2020/08/24/14-32-42-157_58dc4ee50f70e298.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598279537143},{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","title":"This is How Many People Don’t Talk About Their Finances","link":"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14986","description":"<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">With National Financial Awareness Day on August 14th, there are more reasons than ever to be aware of what is going on with your finances. When was the last time that you really looked at your overall financial situation? If you’re like many Americans, the answer to that question may be a long time ago (or even never!). While there is a positive correlation between how closely you look at your finances and your financial health, there are still many people who avoid looking at their finances.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Turbo’s #RealMoneyTalk study</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February 2019, Turbo </span><a href=\"https://www.intuit.com/company/press-room/press-releases/2019/intuit-turbo-launches-realmoneytalk-campaign-featuring-chrissy-metz-to-break-the-taboo-of-talking-about-money/\" target=\"_blank\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">commissioned a survey</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> that was conducted online by The Harris Poll. The aim of the study was to better understand American attitudes and behaviors around discussing their personal finances and money-related topics with others. The study also categorized responses across generations, with a specific focus on Generation Z (those ages 18-23). In this article, we will look at some of the results of that study, with a focus on why people do and do not talk about their finances.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>How many people don’t talk to anyone at their finances</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Turbo #RealMoneyTalk survey showed that more than half (51%) of respondents do not talk about their finances with either their friends OR family. 43% of respondents said they didn’t feel comfortable talking about money or financial status with their friends, while 27% were not comfortable talking about their finances with family.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>How comfortable you are talking about money depends on your age</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The study also shows that the level of comfort that one has in talking about money certainly depends on your age. For many of the questions in the study, the respondents were categorized into one of four different age brackets – Gen Z, Millennials, Gen X and Boomers. There was a distinct pattern based on which age bracket you were in, with younger respondents being more likely to feel comfortable talking about money.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Gen Z (71%) is more likely than Gen X (61%) or Boomers (48%)&nbsp; to say they are comfortable talking about money with friends. Gen Z (67%) is also the most likely to talk about their financial situation with family, as compared to Millennials (52%), Gen X (39%) and Boomers (31%). Interestingly, the opposite trend holds for how comfortable respondents were in talking about money matters with a partner. There, Gen Z (31%) was LEAST likely to feel comfortable (compared to Millennials (43%), Gen X (48%) and Boomers (51%). Perhaps older respondents are on average in longer-lasting relationships where there is more of a level of trust.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Most people did not talk about money growing up</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While the taboo about talking about finances can have many different causes, one may be the environment in which people were raised. The #RealMoneyTalk survey asked how often finances were discussed in your household when you were growing up? Nearly half of respondents (47%) said that money was rarely (32%) or never (15%) discussed. Only 22% of respondents said that money was always or often talked about when they were growing up.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Again, there is a clear generational disparity in the answers to these questions, with younger respondents being more likely to have discussed money matters growing up. Gen Z (74%) and Millennials (67%) are more likely than Gen X (54%) or Boomers (38%) to say that finances were at least sometimes discussed in their household when they were growing up. The data certainly shows that money matters are being talked about more and more these days.</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Talking about debt is a different matter</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While many respondents felt comfortable discussing general money matters, there was a marked decline in the number of respondents who felt comfortable talking about their debt. Specifically, 29% of respondents say that they are embarrassed to talk about how much debt they have, and nearly 1 in 5 Americans (19%) say they have lied about how much debt they have when they are with their friends.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Again, responses vary not only by age but by gender. Women (33%) are slightly more likely than men (25%) to say they are embarrassed to talk about how much debt they have. Boomers (19%) are least likely to say they are embarrassed to talk about how much debt they have, compared to Gen X (33%), Millennials (39%) and Gen Z (35%).</span></p> \n<h3><strong>Why you should talk about your finances</strong></h3> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Pearson’s law states that “when performance is measured, performance improves. When performance is measured and reported back, the rate of improvement accelerates.” The same holds true for your overall financial well-being. It is very unlikely that you will be able to improve your financial situation without knowing what it even is! A good way to start understanding your finances might be as simple as </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/budgeting-3/how-to-create-a-budget-step-by-step\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">starting a budget</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Talking about your finances with a trusted friend or family member can be a great way to improve your situation even more. Of course, you will want to be smart about what information you want to share (and to whom!) but being able to measure and report progress can be a great motivator to put yourself right where you want to be</span></p> \n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com/consumer-iq/this-is-how-many-people-dont-talk-about-their-finances/\">This is How Many People Don’t Talk About Their Finances</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.mint.com\">MintLife Blog</a>.</p> \n<div class=\"feedflare\"> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=fre2rJivbRY:Jk3p_X5QQ8I:D7DqB2pKExk\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=fre2rJivbRY:Jk3p_X5QQ8I:D7DqB2pKExk\" border=\"0\" /></a> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=fre2rJivbRY:Jk3p_X5QQ8I:gIN9vFwOqvQ\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=fre2rJivbRY:Jk3p_X5QQ8I:gIN9vFwOqvQ\" border=\"0\" /></a> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=fre2rJivbRY:Jk3p_X5QQ8I:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=fre2rJivbRY:Jk3p_X5QQ8I:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\" /></a> \n <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=fre2rJivbRY:Jk3p_X5QQ8I:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?i=fre2rJivbRY:Jk3p_X5QQ8I:V_sGLiPBpWU\" <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?a=fre2rJivbRY:Jk3p_X5QQ8I:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\" /></a> \n</div>\n<img 22:32:17","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","title":"Survey: 40% of Americans Feel Late to Financial and Life Milestones","link":"https://blog.mint.com/?p=14898","description":"<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To a certain extent, Americans are raised with expectations of how their lives will go. By 18 you finish high school, and then you choose a job or go to college. By 22 you should be settling down with a clear career plan, considering a family, and contributing to your </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/investing/401k-early-withdrawal/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">401k</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. By 30 you’ll have a comfortable savings, your first home, and your life all figured out.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Part of reaching adulthood is realizing that there is no timeline set in stone for your life, and a thousand factors influence when and if you reach certain milestones. By your late 20s, you’ve figured out that 30 is not a magic number, either. Still, the pressures from the media and what we see our peers achieving can cause us to feel like we don’t measure up, and may even result in some questionable financial choices. So we set out to find just where Americans feel like they’re falling behind in life.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">We surveyed 1,500 Americans on peer pressure and found:</span></p> \n<ul> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The most common answer for Americans feeling behind was that they’re not saving enough for retirement.</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Americans feel more behind on financial goals, like career success and financial stability, than life goals, like finding a partner and starting a family.</span></li> \n <li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">75% of Americans don’t discuss their financial health and details with their friends.&nbsp;</span></li> \n</ul> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Americans Feel Behind Their Peers on Saving for Retirement</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><img style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Concern about retirement savings was the most common worry for the 40 percent of Americans who feel they’re falling behind in life. Retirement is one of the largest investments of one’s lifetime, and often takes decades to prepare for. The sense of falling behind in retirement savings may be heightened as COVID-19 caused layoffs, a loss in job benefits, and financial struggles that led many to dip into their savings.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Saving for retirement is top of mind for those aged 45–54, 43 percent of whom reported feeling behind on their savings goals. This is not much of a surprise considering </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/retirement-plan\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">retirement</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> age begins at age 66, leaving just a decade or two to fill their nest egg.&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Additionally, 66 percent of those who feel behind on retirement savings are women. Our survey found that women were more likely than men to feel like they’re behind their peers, despite the result that women and men are relatively even when it comes to discussing their personal finances with friends.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Americans Feel More Behind on Financial Goals than Relationship Goals</span></h2> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"14900\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/goals/falling-behind-in-life/attachment/overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack.png\" data-orig-size=\"1306,1677\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack.png?w=234\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack.png?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-14900\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack.png\" alt=\"Comparison of when American achieve these life milestones vs. the most concerned ages\" width=\"640\" height=\"822\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack.png 1306w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack.png?resize=768,986 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack.png?resize=1196,1536 1196w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack.png?resize=272,349 272w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-2-how-feelings-stack.png?resize=248,319 248w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">All age groups were far more concerned about their financial goals and wellbeing than they were relationship milestones. This is particularly interesting considering only 25 percent of Americans discuss their financial status with friends, whereas their peers’ relationship statuses are far more visible.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to our study, only 17 percent of Americans feeling behind their peers are concerned about their search for a life partner. Even fewer are concerned about starting a family. While demographics under 30 were more likely to feel behind on relationship goals, financial goals were still a higher priority.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While all age groups prioritize financial goals, these specific wants change with age. As the youngest group with the </span><a href=\"https://www.comparably.com/blog/old-millennials-young-millennials-and-gen-z-comparing-compensation-and-culture/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">lowest income expectations</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, it’s no surprise that 14.8 percent of Gen Z feel as though they’re struggling for financial stability. Millennials feel more secure in their financial wellbeing and seem to be looking for their next investment — </span><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/housing/home-down-payment-savings/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchasing a home</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. This group had the lowest rate of consensus, but 12.9 percent of Millennials agree they’re behind on homeownership.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Older demographics not only compare themselves to their peers less, but also have the same financial priority in mind — saving for retirement. Gen X is the most concerned about their savings with 15 percent believing they’re behind their peers. With less than a decade until retirement, Baby Boomers are equally concerned at 14.9 percent.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<h2><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">75% of Americans Don’t Share Their Financial Standing With Friends</span></h2> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While Americans may be comparing their finances with their peers’, a majority of adults don’t discuss money topics. Of those who are open to money talk, 11 percent have shared their salary — a relatively popular topic with Gen X-ers, of whom 23 percent talk pay. </span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><img data-attachment-id=\"14901\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/goals/falling-behind-in-life/attachment/overcome-time-anxiety-3-what-americans-willing-to-share/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-3-what-americans-willing-to-share.png\" data-orig-size=\"1306,1507\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"overcome-time-anxiety-3-what-americans-willing-to-share\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-3-what-americans-willing-to-share.png?w=260\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-3-what-americans-willing-to-share.png?w=1306\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone size-full wp-image-14901\" style=\"font-family: -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, 'Segoe UI', Roboto, Oxygen-Sans, Ubuntu, Cantarell, 'Helvetica Neue', sans-serif;\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-3-what-americans-willing-to-share.png\" alt=\"Bar graph of what financial topics Americans are sharing with friends\" width=\"640\" height=\"738\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-3-what-americans-willing-to-share.png 1306w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-3-what-americans-willing-to-share.png?resize=768,886 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-3-what-americans-willing-to-share.png?resize=302,349 302w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/overcome-time-anxiety-3-what-americans-willing-to-share.png?resize=276,319 276w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /></span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the flip side, just six percent of Americans share their </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/how-mint-works/credit\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">credit score</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. This could be in part because </span><a href=\"https://consumerfed.org/press_release/survey-shows-an-increasing-number-of-consumers-have-obtained-their-credit-scores-and-know-much-more-about-credit-scores/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">43 percent</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> of Americans haven’t checked their credit score in more than a year.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If adults aren’t discussing their financial standing, then it’s likely that the peer pressure so many feel is a result of time anxiety more than actual, documented success. There’s a perception that adults should hit certain milestones by certain phases of life, and there’s a sense of anxiety we feel when we recognize that the deadline is looming.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This reinforces the expectation that we shouldn’t discuss our finances, either because we don’t want to feel like we’re bragging or because we don’t feel comfortable sharing our real or perceived struggles. In fact, the taboo is so strong that in </span><a href=\"https://www.fidelity.com/bin-public/060_www_fidelity_com/documents/pr/couples-fact-sheet.pdf\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">34 percent</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> of couples living together, at least one partner doesn’t know how much the other makes.&nbsp;</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The good thing is that there is no real timeline for our lives. There may be averages or societal expectations, but meeting or missing these “due dates” doesn’t define success, and certainly says nothing about one’s individual value.</span></p> \n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s natural to compare yourself with your peers, but it becomes a problem when the feeling of falling behind crosses into time anxiety territory. The best thing you can do to control your financial success is </span><a href=\"https://www.mint.com/how-mint-works/budgets\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">budget</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> well and focus on your own success while reducing the influence from others. While it may feel overwhelming, here are some great ways to manage your time anxiety and take control of your own timeline.</span></p> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/how-to-overcome-time-anxiety-infographic-2.png\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><img data-attachment-id=\"14902\" ://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn38@2020_5/2020/08/24/14-32-43-084_e538087722dd60e5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/MyMint?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn17@2020_3/2020/08/24/14-32-43-174_4a59b36f6bebab35.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/MyMint/~4/NdJezM6X450":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn53@2020_6/2020/08/24/14-32-42-165_4d6eba1b4695294d.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598279537141},{"createdTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","updatedTime":"2020-08-24 22:32:17","title":"How to Prepare for a Recession: 8 Tips You Can Start Now","link":"https://blog.mint.com/?p=15007","description":"<p>A recession can impact your everyday life and budget, but there are things you can do to prepare. As of June 2020, the COVID-19 pandemic showed a possibility of a recession, with <a href=\"https://www.dol.gov/sites/dolgov/files/OPA/newsreleases/ui-claims/20201364.pdf\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">33 million unemployed Americans</a> inquiring about jobless benefits. During tough times, it’s normal to feel anxious about your lifestyle, career, and budget. Even if things improve and a recession never comes, practicing responsible <a href=\"https://www.mint.com/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">money habits</a> can only set you up for success.</p> \n<p>Start implementing healthy budgeting habits to prepare for any financial opportunities or emergencies. Before diving into how to prepare for a recession, let’s review what typically happens in one.</p> \n<h2>What Is a Recession?</h2> \n<p>A recession is an economic downturn that occurs over a period of time where unemployment rises, and trade and industrial activity decline. While it can vary, a recession typically refers to six or more consecutive months of economic decline. This means a country’s gross domestic product (GDP) declines for two back-to-back quarters, signaling slower or negative economic growth.</p> \n<p>After an 11-year economic growth period in the U.S., the COVID-19 pandemic recently caused a downturn, sparking fears of a recession. While these last few quarters were in the red, the U.S. economy is projected to upswing towards the <a href=\"https://www.goldmansachs.com/insights/pages/us-daily-20-march-2020.html\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">end of 2020</a>.</p> \n<h3>Recession vs. Depression: What’s the Difference?</h3> \n<p>A recession and depression are commonly confused. Think of it this way: a recession is a short-term regional economic downturn, while a depression is a more severe long-term regional or global economic downturn.</p> \n<ul> \n <li>A <strong>recession</strong> shows a negative turn in the economy, primarily affecting employment and production. This means the average household income and spending decreases across a country. In a recession, these spending patterns continue in one country for <a href=\"https://www.nber.org/cycles.html\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">six months and up to 3.5 years</a>. In the event of a recession, your family may hold off on making any large purchases, like buying a new car or house.</li> \n <li>A <strong>depression</strong> is a widespread increase in unemployment and a pause in economic activity across a region, and it can even spread globally. This includes a decrease in construction, world trade, and capital movements affecting the business cycle for <a href=\"https://www.investopedia.com/terms/d/depression.asp\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">three or more</a> straight years. For instance, the Great Depression lasted almost a decade with ongoing negative growth across the globe. During that time, many families were unemployed for years on end.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Given the different ramifications of an economic downturn, either type can be detrimental to your lifestyle. Not knowing the length or long-term effects of a recession or depression may increase your anxiety. To get ahead of financial emergencies, it’s helpful to always be prepared. Read what normally happens during a recession and how to prepare in the sections below.</p> \n<h3>What Typically Happens in a Recession?</h3> \n<p>During a recession, countrywide household and business spending are restricted for two or more quarters of the year. During that time, the decrease in spending leads to large-scale layoffs and rapidly increasing unemployment. These changes generally carry out in a given country for months to a few years.</p> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"15009\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/planning/how-to-prepare-for-a-recession/attachment/how-to-prepare-yourself-for-a-recession/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/How-to-Prepare-Yourself-for-a-Recession.png\" data-orig-size=\"2612,1376\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"How to Prepare Yourself for a Recession\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/How-to-Prepare-Yourself-for-a-Recession.png?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/How-to-Prepare-Yourself-for-a-Recession.png?w=2612\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-15009 size-full\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/How-to-Prepare-Yourself-for-a-Recession.png\" alt=\"How to Prepare Yourself for a Recession\" width=\"2612\" height=\"1376\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/How-to-Prepare-Yourself-for-a-Recession.png 2612w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/How-to-Prepare-Yourself-for-a-Recession.png?resize=768,405 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/How-to-Prepare-Yourself-for-a-Recession.png?resize=1536,809 1536w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/How-to-Prepare-Yourself-for-a-Recession.png?resize=2048,1079 2048w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/How-to-Prepare-Yourself-for-a-Recession.png?resize=662,349 662w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/How-to-Prepare-Yourself-for-a-Recession.png?resize=606,319 606w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2612px) 100vw, 2612px\" /></p> \n<h2>How to Prepare Yourself for a Recession</h2> \n<p>Whether a recession is approaching or not, there are ways to plan your budget for any economic changes. Building your savings, re-evaluating <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/planning/investment-calculator/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">investments</a>, and managing debts are key opportunities to get ahead of any unexpected events. Always keep your budget prepared with our go-to tips below.</p> \n<h3>1. Reassess Your Budget Monthly</h3> \n<p>Evaluate your <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/how-to-budget/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">budget</a> every month to see what expenses could be kicked to the curb. Are you spending too much on clothes? Cut them out. Only buy what you need and opt for generic over name-brand products to save a couple extra dollars.</p> \n<h3>2. Contribute More Towards Your Emergency Fund</h3> \n<p>After cutting out unnecessary expenses, increase your savings budget as much as you can. Ideally, 20 percent of your income should go to your savings, and 30 percent to “extra” expenses like your subscriptions and memberships. After slimming down your extra expenses, set up higher automatic payments to your emergency fund. If you lose your job or have car troubles, you’ll have your <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/how-to-reevaluate-your-emergency-fund-strategy/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">emergency fund</a> there to help out.</p> \n<h3>3. Focus on Paying Off High-Interest Debt Accounts</h3> \n<p>Track each debt account you have using <a href=\"https://www.mint.com/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">our app</a> to see how much you owe and your various interest rates. Focus on contributing more of your income to debt that holds the highest interest rates. While doing so, consider paying off <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/debt/10-steps-to-paying-off-your-debt/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">tax deductible</a> debt accounts, like educational loans, to get cash back during tax season.</p> \n<h3>4. Keep Up With Your Usual Contributions</h3> \n<p>Whether you already have a <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/investing/401k-contribution-limits/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">401k set up</a> or not, try to maintain your budgeted contributions. It can be intimidating to put money in while a recession is looming, but keeping up with these can benefit you in the long-term. During volatile times, try to avoid checking your performance each day to stay at ease with your future goals in mind.</p> \n<h3>5. Evaluate Your Investment Choices</h3> \n<p>Whether your <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/investing/low-risk-investments/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">investments</a> are doing well or not, avoid making emotional money decisions. If the market takes a turn for the worse, consider riding it out for any upswings. Reach out to a <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/financial-literacy/how-to-find-and-vet-a-financial-advisor/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">trusted financial advisor</a> before making any huge changes.</p> \n<h3>6. Build Up Skills On Your Resume</h3> \n<p>Use free online learning platforms like YouTube, expert guides, LinkedIn courses, and assessments to boost your resume. Show off your skills during meetings to show your employer your value. Add every certificate you earn along the way to your resume — this will help prove your eagerness to learn. Increasing your skills could, in turn, increase your value and <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/early-career/increase-your-earning-potential/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">earning potential</a>.</p> \n<h3>7. Brainstorm Innovative Ways to Make Extra Cash</h3> \n<p>Whether things are heading towards a recession or not, consider starting a passion project to bring in supplemental income. Invest time in creating an ebook, online course, or blog on a skill that you’ve mastered and could use to earn <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/planning/passive-income-ideas/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">passive income</a>. Directly deposit your side hustle earnings into your savings account for an extra financial cushion.</p> \n<h3>8. Prioritize Online and In-Person Networking Events</h3> \n<p>Master your digital and in-person networking skills by attending networking events each month. Meet with industry professionals to offer your skills, learn from them, and establish long-lasting business connections. Down the road, these connections could open up career opportunities or expert-level business advice.</p> \n<h2>Mistakes to Avoid During a Recession</h2> \n<p><img data-attachment-id=\"15010\" data-permalink=\"https://blog.mint.com/planning/how-to-prepare-for-a-recession/attachment/mistakes-to-avoid-during-a-recession/\" data-orig-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mistakes-to-Avoid-During-a-Recession.png\" data-orig-size=\"2612,2148\" data-comments-opened=\"1\" data-image-meta=\"{&quot;aperture&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;credit&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;camera&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;caption&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;created_timestamp&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;copyright&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;focal_length&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;iso&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;shutter_speed&quot;:&quot;0&quot;,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;orientation&quot;:&quot;0&quot;}\" data-image-title=\"Mistakes to Avoid During a Recession\" data-image-description=\"\" data-medium-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mistakes-to-Avoid-During-a-Recession.png?w=300\" data-large-file=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mistakes-to-Avoid-During-a-Recession.png?w=2612\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"alignnone wp-image-15010 size-full\" src=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mistakes-to-Avoid-During-a-Recession.png\" alt=\"Mistakes to Avoid During a Recession\" width=\"2612\" height=\"2148\" srcset=\"https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mistakes-to-Avoid-During-a-Recession.png 2612w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mistakes-to-Avoid-During-a-Recession.png?resize=768,632 768w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mistakes-to-Avoid-During-a-Recession.png?resize=1536,1263 1536w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mistakes-to-Avoid-During-a-Recession.png?resize=2048,1684 2048w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mistakes-to-Avoid-During-a-Recession.png?resize=424,349 424w, https://blog.mint.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Mistakes-to-Avoid-During-a-Recession.png?resize=388,319 388w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2612px) 100vw, 2612px\" /></p> \n<p>During an economic downturn, avoid putting your finances at risk and prepare for any emergencies. Here are some common mistakes you’ll want to avoid:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Panicking</strong>: Steer clear of fear. If sudden changes spark anxiety, take a deep breath and see if there’s an upswing shortly after. If you’re unsure of any economic changes, reach out to a <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/financial-literacy/how-to-find-and-vet-a-financial-advisor/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">financial advisor</a>.</li> \n <li><strong>Increasing your debt</strong>: Even though recessions may lower interest rates on <a href=\"https://www.mint.com/resources/loan-calculator/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">loans</a>, avoid taking on more debt. Instead, focus on paying off any debt you already have.</li> \n <li><strong>Becoming a cosigner</strong>: In the event the primary debt holder isn’t able to make a payment, the cosigner is held responsible. To avoid taking on more potential debt, stay away from cosigning.</li> \n <li><strong>Taking your job for granted</strong>: Whether you want to stay at your job for a while or not, always showcase your skills. During an economic downturn, highlight these skills and put off quitting until you have another opportunity lined up.</li> \n <li><strong>Not building an emergency fund:</strong> You may need supplemental income for your daily necessities and unexpected events. Build up your emergency fund so you can cover at least three to six months of your expenses.</li> \n <li><strong>Taking on more fixed expenses</strong>: Focus on decreasing your overall expenses. Evaluate what you can eliminate from your budget and avoid increasing your fixed expenses, like a new car payment or an expensive apartment.</li> \n <li><strong>Not having a backup plan</strong>: First, create a <a href=\"https://www.mint.com/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">budget</a> that works for you and adjust as you go. Update your resume, save extra cash, or start a side hustle for extra backup opportunities in case things take an unexpected turn.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>No matter the state of the economy, practicing these healthy financial strategies can help improve your budget and opportunities. The best way to increase your savings and prepare for unexpected events is to <a href=\"https://www.mint.com/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">track your budget</a>, frequently adjust it, build up your <a href=\"https://blog.mint.com/saving/how-to-reevaluate-your-emergency-fund-strategy/\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"false noopener noreferrer\">emergency fund</a>, and seek opportunities to improve your experience. Level up your savings accounts and career while practicing good financial habits.</p> \n<p><strong>Sources</strong>: <a href=\"https://www.merriam-webster.com/words-at-play/economic-recession-vs-depression-difference#:~:text=A%20recession%20is%20a%20downtrend,major%20pauses%20in%20economic%20activity.\" title=\"\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Merriam-Webster 1</a>, <a href=\"https://www.merriam-webster.com/words-at-play/economic-recession-vs-depression-difference\" title=\"\"
